                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-111899337861">
                      Savory Rosemary and Goat Cheese Muffin Recipe
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-111899337861" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                           <span class="author-name Font-C-2-140 D-b">
                            <a class="attribution-name Font-C-2-140 Fw-b Whs-n" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:7bb30252-80bb-30e6-810a-dfcb78304600;t9:17;elm:itm;elmt:link;itc:0" href="http://www.alwaysorderdessert.com" style="color:#000;" target="_blank">
                             Alejandra Ramos
                            </a>
                           </span>
                           <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            <span>
                             March 5, 2015
                            </span>
                           </time>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-111899337861" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Every week, were
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:7bb30252-80bb-30e6-810a-dfcb78304600;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/food/tagged/blogger-of-the-week" target="_blank">
                            spotlighting a different food blogger
                           </a>
                           whos shaking up the blogosphere with tempting recipes and knockout photography. Here, Alejandra Ramos of
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:7bb30252-80bb-30e6-810a-dfcb78304600;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.alwaysorderdessert.com/" target="_blank">
                            Always Order Dessert
                           </a>
                           shares a savory goat cheese muffin recipe that sounds pretty darn appealing any time of day.
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="Savory Rosemary and Goat Cheese Muffin Recipe" height="375" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/27ec84f3b26babe607c125fbb9fc896ad33347d7.jpg" width="500"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Photo: Alejandra Ramos
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Savory Rosemary and Chvre Muffins
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          Makes about 2 dozen
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           These ridiculously easy and tasty savory muffinswhich Ive stuffed with chunks of fresh chvre, sauted red onions, and sprigs of rosemaryarea snap to make.
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Theyre perfect to serve at parties alongside a cheese plate, to keep guests entertained while you finish up dinner (or your makeup). They also freeze well and can be made well ahead of time. Serve them warm straight from the oven or at room temperature. Theyre also yummy with eggs the next morning!
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          1 tablespoon butter, plus more for buttering tins
                          <br/>
                          1 small red onion, minced
                          <br/>
                          Vegetable oil or nonstick cooking oil spray
                          <br/>
                          12/3 cup all purpose flour
                          <br/>
                          1 tablespoon baking powder
                          <br/>
                          1 teaspoon kosher salt
                          <br/>
                          2 large eggs
                          <br/>
                          1 cup whole milk
                          <br/>
                          2 tablespoons sour cream or plain yogurt
                          <br/>
                          2/3 cup fresh goat cheese (plain or herbed), broken into small 1/2 chunks
                          <br/>
                          4 teaspoons chopped fresh rosemary, plus 24 small sprigs for garnishing (garnish optional)
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Begin by melting the butter in a small saucepan and sauting the onion for about 5-8 minutes, or until soft and just slightly caramelized. Allow onions to cool.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Pre-heat the oven to 400F. Grease your mini muffin pan well with oil or pan spray, or line with mini muffin liners.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Sift the flour, baking powder, and salt into a large bowl. In a separate bowl, beat one egg, then whisk in milk and sour cream or yogurt. Add the egg mixture to the flour mixture and stir gently just until combined. (Dont worry if there are a few small lumps.)
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Gently fold the cooked onion, goat cheese, and chopped rosemary into the muffin batter. (Reserve the sprigs).
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Spoon the mixture straight into greased mini muffin tins until it just about reaches the top.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Beat the second egg with a tablespoon of water and brush each of the muffin surfaces, then, if you like, insert a small sprig of rosemary in the center of each one.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Bake about 20 minutes, or until risen and just slightly golden and a toothpick inserted into the largest muffin comes out clean. (A bit of melted goat cheese may stick to the tester, but no batter should.)
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Let cool for two minutes before gently removing to a rack to continue cooling.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Serve warm or room temperature. If you want to store, freeze the muffins and then let defrost at room temperature for two hours before serving. You may also reheat briefly in a 350 degree oven.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Have a hankering for muffins? More to try:
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:7bb30252-80bb-30e6-810a-dfcb78304600;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/food/kale-and-goat-cheese-muffins-98486339056.html" target="_blank">
                           Kale and goat cheese muffins for breakfast
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:7bb30252-80bb-30e6-810a-dfcb78304600;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/food/a-doughnut-muffin-hybrid-yes-please-84235331611.html" target="_blank">
                           A doughnut-muffin hybrid to haunt your dreams
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:7bb30252-80bb-30e6-810a-dfcb78304600;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/food/blueberry-oatmeal-muffins-with-flaxseed-72455514927.html" target="_blank">
                           Blueberry oatmeal muffins chock full of flaxseed
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           How do you like your muffinssweet or savory? Tell us below!
                          </i>
                         </p>

Couple Quit Their Full-Time Jobs to Sell Farm-Fresh Peaches","summary":"Stephen and Jessica Rose from The Peach Truck, (Photo: Lily Glass) When Stephen Rose was trying to persuade his Seattle-born girlfriend Jessica to move to Nashville, he convinced her of some of the South virtues: front porches, lakes and sweet, juicy peaches.  They decided if they were willing to drive across state lines to get these peaches, other Nashville residents could become converts.  Photo: Lily Glass They also started knocking on the doors of restaurants, offering to supply them with Georgia peaches, from Pearson Farm, a fifth-generation peach farm run by a couple who were close family friends.  The business has now expanded to include 50 peach slingers who work across Nashville selling peaches for $8 for a 3-pound bag, a team of five who sell peaches throughout Kentucky, Tennessee, Ohio, and Indiana, and an Internet-sales business.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fd7e284263e046a136a35b5b5aa40650ad8b8c7c4.jpg\" alt=\"This Couple Quit Their Full-Time Jobs to Sell Farm-Fresh Peaches\" width=\"540\" height=\"521\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EStephen and Jessica Rose from The Peach Truck, (Photo: Lily Glass)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen Stephen Rose was trying to persuade his Seattle-born girlfriend Jessica to move to Nashville, he convinced her of some of the South virtues: front porches, lakes and sweet, juicy peaches.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe problem was once he moved, he couldn&#x2019;t find any.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo solve what the couple dubbed &#x201C;the peach problem,&#x201D; Rose drove to Georgia, where he grew up, and picked a peach to show Jessica what all the fuss was about. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThey decided if they were willing to drive across state lines to get these peaches, other Nashville residents could become converts. The couple married, and when they got back from their honeymoon in the summer of 2012, they started selling from a truck peaches that had been picked the day before and driven over from Georgia.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"537\" height=\"810\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w537\u002Fea8aee0a47c9b0611093079b7a08057fafbe7268.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPhoto: Lily Glass\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThey also started knocking on the doors of restaurants, offering to supply them with Georgia peaches, from Pearson Farm, a fifth-generation peach farm run by a couple who were close family friends. Stephen and Jessica were so successful that the couple started seriously considering quitting their full-time jobs.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I felt like at 26, I was signing up for the rest of my life to this monotonous daily corporate grind,&#x201D; says Rose, who worked in corporate sales. &#x201C;We got to talking, and said what if we give up our summers &#x2014; and our summers are insane &#x2014; but literally have five months to do whatever we want to do.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBy the summer of 2013 they took the plunge. The business has now expanded to include 50 &#x201C;peach slingers&#x201D; who work across Nashville selling peaches for $8 for a 3-pound bag, a team of five who sell peaches throughout Kentucky, Tennessee, Ohio, and Indiana, and an \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthepeachtruck.com\u002Fproducts\u002Fpeach-box\"\u003EInternet-sales business\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. They now sell more than one million peaches a season.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"438\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F521b00c991ed2dc83a95c2d463e0b7cc993f1755.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPeaches packed for shipping; Photo: Jamie Clayton\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOne reason these are the best peaches you&#x2019;ll ever have, Rose boasts, is because the Peach Truck only focuses on one item, as opposed to grocery stores, which deal with thousands.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAlso, it&#x2019;s supply chain is much more direct. By the time a peach makes it into the hands of a grocery store customer, it&#x2019;s gone from the farm to a central distribution center, then onto a local center. Once it&#x2019;s in the grocery store, it sits in the back until they need to restock. That means weeks in between ripening on the tree and ending up on a buyer&#x2019;s hand.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe Peach Truck gets peaches that are picked in the morning, packed in the afternoon, and then put on a truck are ready for sale the next day. All that &#x201C;extra&#x201D; time on the tree makes a big difference in flavor.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhy are these peaches superior? Geography and climate play a huge roll in how a peach tastes, Rose says. Georgia soil is dense red clay that holds nutrients right below the surface. During the summer, heat can hover and 95 degrees and humid during the day &#x2014; and only getting down to about 80 degrees at night.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"354\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F52beb389bd41f862290aa273a80f3445fe361357.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EJessica and Stephen Rose talking with customers; Photo: Lily Glass\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s miserably hot, and that peach is suffering, day and night,&#x201D; Rose says. &#x201C;But that suffering builds up that sugar content and you get that sweet, juicy peach you dream about.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EJosh Habiger, the chef at Pinewood Social and the culinary director for \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fstrategichospitalityonline.com\u002F\"\u003EStrategic Hospitality\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which operates a few Nashville restaurants including \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fthecatbirdseatrestaurant.com\u002F\"\u003EThe Catbird Seat\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, was one of the chefs that the Roses approached.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;This dude showed up one day, and says, &#x2018;Hey man, we drove our truck down and have some peaches and they were handing them out old-school style,&#x201D; Habiger says. &#x201C;Now, everyone in the restaurant business here is aware of the peach truck, everyone uses their peaches.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAt his restaurants, the peaches are making appearances in dishes like a peach and burrata salad at \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpinewoodsocial.com\u002F\"\u003EPinewood Social\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and oysters with a peach mignonette at the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.thepattersonnashville.com\u002F\"\u003EPatterson House\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Right now we&#x2019;re at the peak where peaches are just perfect,&#x201D; Habiger says. &#x201C;You take a bite and it just runs down your face.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFellow chef Sean Brock, who is behind \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.huskrestaurant.com\u002F\"\u003EHusk\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the famed restaurant with locations in Charleston and Nashville came across the Peach Truck while at a farmers market.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I could smell the peaches a mile away,&#x201D; Brock says, and sought out the couple to learn more.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBrock liked that the peaches were produced in a way that preserved sustainable farming traditions from multiple generations. The farm isn&#x2019;t certified organic &#x2014; the humid southeast can make bugs a problem &#x2014; but pesticides are only used as a last-line of defense, and care is taken to make sure the soil is full of nutrients for next year&#x2019;s crop.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s rare for peach farmers to follow old-fashioned and sustainable ways of raising them because it&#x2019;s very difficult,&#x201D; Brock says. &#x201C;But you can smell and taste the difference.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"403\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fd81187500cd91e038eccc1e567d53fd80025136c.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe peach crop now is a worry for Rose, because his growing family, which now includes a baby daughter, depends on it. He says they live more simply in order to have more free time in the off-season, and they also save up for the future because they don&#x2019;t know what the next growing season will look like. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd while several months off a year to travel sounds amazing &#x2014; and the Roses plan to take their daughter and travel through Spain, Portugal and Morocco &#x2014; the down time isn&#x2019;t all vacation. Rose has picked up other jobs, including driving for Uber, in the off-season.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe couple is also trying to make the most of this one and expand further afield. On Friday, the Roses are coming to New York City for stops at farmers and food markets.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E Rose can&#x2019;t wait to see New Yorkers&#x2019; reactions. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I&#x2019;ve seen people bite in and get tears in their eyes, and say, &#x2018;I remember when I was a kid and tasted peaches like this, and I haven&#x2019;t in years,&#x2019;&#x201D; Rose says. &#x201C;I think a lot of people in New York will have that same reaction and it&#x2019;s pretty thrilling.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECraving more peaches? the Great Depression Created the Double Popsicle","summary":"The popsicle was allegedly invented by an 11-year-old named Frank Epperson who left his drink and a stirrer outside on a cold California night.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fcdbe8ae8eda3f88f1e72304b26fe70ddfa51c301.jpg\" alt=\"How the Great Depression Created the Double Popsicle\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Csmall\u003EPhoto courtesy of People&#x2019;s Pops.\u003C\u002Fsmall\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBy Annie Quigley\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe popsicle was allegedly invented by an 11-year-old named Frank Epperson who left his drink and a stirrer outside on a cold California night. But what about the double popsicle? Who first decided that two are better than one?\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAfter Epperson&#x2019;s 1905 boyhood discovery and his (somewhat belated) public patent in 1923, the frozen treat&#x2019;s popularity skyrocketed. But it was several years later, when the Great Depression hit, that the Popsicle company started freezing pops together and selling two for the price of one. For just a nickel, families that were short on cash could buy one treat, split it, and feed two kids. And so the double ice pop became a delicious yet practical pick-me-up to bolster American spirits.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESo, it turns out we&#x2019;ve been eating double popsicles wrong this whole time, but it&#x2019;s okay; they&#x2019;re tough to share. Epicurious\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg height=\"240\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECamping is all about the skills&#x2014;the skills needed to trudge through the woods (where you might meet a bear!), the skills needed to build a fire.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut while the ability to gather tinder, read a compass, and sip from a flask in the dark is important, even crucial, the most important skill comes into play before you even hit the trail: The 8-step process of packing food in a cooler.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ERelated:\u003Cb\u003E \u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.epicurious.com\u002Fingredients\u002F14-ways-to-eat-salmon-for-dinner-tonight-gallery?mbid=synd_yfood\"\u003E14 No-Stress Ways to Cook Salmon\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E1. GATHER EVERYTHING YOU NEED\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOnce you have the menu for your trip planned, map out exactly how much of each ingredient you&#x2019;ll need for every recipe and prep as much as you can for each meal in advance. Prep any vegetables you&#x2019;ll need, marinate your meats, pre-package hobo packs for breakfast, pack up small containers for condiments, and don&#x2019;t forget the salt. (Seriously. Do \u003Ci\u003Enot\u003C\u002Fi\u003E forget the salt.) Because everything you pack in the cooler is probably going to get wet, make sure to package everything in leak-proof resealable containers or plastic bags.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E2. SCORE THE RIGHT STORAGE\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe thicker the walls, the better insulated the cooler&#x2014;and the longer it&#x2019;ll keep things cold. But it&#x2019;s not just the walls that matter: you want to make sure your cooler has a thick, well-insulated lid. If yours doesn&#x2019;t, you can help it out by packing a thick towel on top of everything under the lid. Also pay attention to how the cooler closes: Any lid that locks in place will help preserve the chilly temperature. We&#x2019;re fans of the tough, super-insulated, bear-proof (and very stylish) coolers from Yeti.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E3. START WITH A COOL COOLER\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECoolers are built to retain temperature, whether it&#x2019;s hot \u003Ci\u003Eor\u003C\u002Fi\u003E cold. So if you store your cooler in the hot attic of your house or the hot garage, make sure you bring it in the house and open it up to air out a day before packing it. Ideally, you&#x2019;ll want to get it cold. DJ Bell, the director of product marketing from Yeti Coolers, recommends dumping a &#x201C;sacrificial&#x201D; bag of ice in your empty cooler to chill it for at least a few hours before packing it. (Discard that ice before you start packing&#x2014;it&#x2019;s done its job.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E4. CHILL WHAT YOU&#x2019;LL BE PACKING\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe colder the food and drink you put into a cooler, the longer it&#x2019;ll stay cold. Makes sense, right? So don&#x2019;t pack warm beers in your cooler: they&#x2019;ll just make everything else in there warm up and make the ice melt faster. Pre-chill everything before you pack, or, even better, pre-\u003Ci\u003Efreeze\u003C\u002Fi\u003E it. Need to pack drinking water? Freeze it. Packing steak? Freeze it in its marinade in a leek-proof bag.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E5. SCORE A MIX OF ICE\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor a one night trip, a couple reusable ice packs will do the trick, and will help keep things less messy. But for a longer haul, you need real ice. When you go to buy that ice, Bell wants you to &#x201C;be an ice snob&#x201D; and be choosy about which bags of ice you buy. He suggests that you &#x201C;Don&#x2019;t get the stuff at the front of the freezer&#x2014;get the stuff that&#x2019;s like a solid block at the back of the freezer.&#x201D; The bigger the ice chunks, the more slowly they&#x2019;ll melt.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E6. PLAN FOR A LONG HAUL\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFirst off, consider using multiple coolers, especially if you&#x2019;re feeding a larger crowd. If you can, use a separate cooler for drinks and a separate cooler for food. (The drinks cooler will probably get opened more often, keeping the more temperature-sensitive food cooler colder, longer.) If you&#x2019;re feeding a big group, you could even have a cooler for each day so you don&#x2019;t need to open up the cooler for your third day until the time comes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you&#x2019;re packing enough food for a weekend trip, you&#x2019;ll want a mix of small ice cubes to chill things quickly, and big blocks to make the chill last longer. You can even throw in one or two reusable cooler packs (we like the ones with a freezing temp below that of water), which will help keep the ice cubes frozen longer.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ERelated:\u003Cb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.epicurious.com\u002Frecipes-menus\u002Fcool-drinks-for-hot-days-recipes-gallery?mbid=synd_yfood\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E11 Cold and Colorful Drinks for Hot Days\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E7. PACK IN LAYERS\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen you start packing, start with a layer of ice on the bottom, then start adding in the items you need to stay coolest (like raw meat) on the bottom. Add another layer of ice, more food, and then more ice. Finish with foods that don&#x2019;t need much refrigeration, like vegetables. If you don&#x2019;t have a separate drinks cooler, pack your drinks on top, since they&#x2019;re the least perishable and will probably be the first thing you go digging for when you set up camp.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E8. KEEP YOUR COOLER&#x2019;S COOL\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ERemember: Air is the enemy in your cooler. If you have even a little bit of space at the top once you&#x2019;re done packing, throw in that towel. And once you get that cooler to camp, try and keep it out of direct sunlight, and resist the urge to open it more than necessary (without sacrificing your intake of beer, of course).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from Epicurious:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.epicurious.com\u002Frecipes-menus\u002Fvegetarian-salads-for-dinner-recipes-gallery?mbid=synd_yfood\"\u003E14 Main Course-Worthy Vegetarian Rosemary and Goat Cheese Muffin Recipe","summary":"Alejandra Ramos of Always Order Dessert shares a savory goat cheese muffin recipe that sounds pretty darn appealing any time of day.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E&#xA0;Every week, we&#x2019;re \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Ftagged\u002Fblogger-of-the-week\"\u003Espotlighting a different food blogger\u003C\u002Fa\u003E who&#x2019;s shaking up the blogosphere with tempting recipes and knockout photography. Here, Alejandra Ramos of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.alwaysorderdessert.com\u002F\"\u003EAlways Order Dessert\u003C\u002Fa\u003E shares a savory goat cheese muffin recipe that sounds pretty darn appealing any time of day.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F27ec84f3b26babe607c125fbb9fc896ad33347d7.jpg\" alt=\"Savory Rosemary and Goat Cheese Muffin Recipe\" width=\"500\" height=\"375\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPhoto: Alejandra Ramos\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESavory Rosemary and Ch&#xE8;vre Muffins\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EMakes about 2 dozen\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThese ridiculously easy and tasty savory muffins&#x2014;which I&#x2019;ve stuffed with chunks of fresh ch&#xE8;vre, saut&#xE9;ed red onions, and sprigs of rosemary&#x2014;are&#xA0;a snap to make.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThey&#x2019;re perfect to serve at parties alongside a cheese plate, to keep guests entertained while you finish up dinner (or your makeup). They also freeze well and can be made well ahead of time. Serve them warm straight from the oven or at room temperature. They&#x2019;re also yummy with eggs the next morning!\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E1 tablespoon butter, plus more for buttering tins\u003Cbr\u003E1 small red onion, minced\u003Cbr\u003EVegetable oil or nonstick cooking oil spray\u003Cbr\u003E1&#xA0;2\u002F3 cup all purpose flour\u003Cbr\u003E1 tablespoon baking powder\u003Cbr\u003E1 teaspoon kosher salt \u003Cbr\u003E2 large eggs\u003Cbr\u003E1 cup whole milk\u003Cbr\u003E2 tablespoons sour cream or plain yogurt\u003Cbr\u003E2\u002F3 cup fresh goat cheese (plain or herbed), broken into small 1\u002F2&#x201D; chunks \u003Cbr\u003E 4 teaspoons chopped fresh rosemary, plus 24 small sprigs for garnishing (garnish optional)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBegin by melting the butter in a small saucepan and saut&#xE9;ing the onion for about 5-8 minutes, or until soft and just slightly caramelized. Allow onions to cool.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPre-heat the oven to 400&#xB0;F. Grease your mini muffin pan well with oil or pan spray, or line with mini muffin liners.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESift the flour, baking powder, and salt into a large bowl. In a separate bowl, beat one egg, then whisk in milk and sour cream or yogurt. Add the egg mixture to the flour mixture and stir gently just until combined. (Don&#x2019;t worry if there are a few small lumps.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EGently fold the cooked onion, goat cheese, and chopped rosemary into the muffin batter. (Reserve the sprigs).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESpoon the mixture straight into greased mini muffin tins until it just about reaches the top.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBeat the second egg with a tablespoon of water and brush each of the muffin surfaces, then, if you like, insert a small sprig of rosemary in the center of each one.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBake about 20 minutes, or until risen and just slightly golden and a toothpick inserted into the largest muffin comes out clean. (A bit of melted goat cheese may stick to the tester, but no batter should.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELet cool for two minutes before gently removing to a rack to continue cooling.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EServe warm or room temperature. If you want to store, freeze the muffins and then let defrost at room temperature for two hours before serving. You may also reheat briefly in a 350 degree oven. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EHave a hankering for muffins?
